## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical rate laws in chemical kinetics relate reaction rates to powers of concentration, and time-dependence may arise from external forcing or coupled species whose concentrations are implicit functions of time.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions, equilibrium shift)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis where product catalyzes reaction)
- Second-order with stoichiometric constraint: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - c2 * A) (two-reactant second-order with one eliminated via stoichiometry)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Cubic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A**3 (polynomial rate law from complex mechanisms)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional-order kinetics with background source/sink)
- Sigmoidal cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) suggests autonomous ODE rate law; if t appears, suspect time-varying external conditions or implicit coupling to other species
- Integer power of A (1, 2, 3) corresponds to molecularity of elementary reaction steps; non-integer powers suggest complex or effective mechanisms
- Negative dA_dt with positive A indicates consumption/decay; sign of leading coefficient encodes whether species is reactant or product
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate enzyme or catalytic saturation where the rate plateaus at high concentration
- Product terms like A*(c-A) arise from stoichiometric coupling where a second species B is expressed as B = c - A via conservation law
- Polynomial rate laws (sum of A powers) often emerge from quasi-steady-state elimination of intermediate species in multi-step mechanisms
- If the rate law involves both A and t multiplicatively (e.g., A*f(t)), this suggests a time-modulated rate constant such as from varying temperature or light intensity
- Cubic or higher-order terms in A can indicate bistability or oscillatory chemical dynamics (e.g., Belousov-Zhabotinsky type)

`-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

This has three terms:
1. A linear term in A: `-0.25667*A`
2. An exponential decay term: `-0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t)`
3. A sinusoidal term: `0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

Let me look for candidates that have `A*exp(c*t)`, a linear `A` term, and `sin(log(A + c))`.

**Candidate 19**: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2 + c3/(A + c4)**2 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`

This has:
- `A*c0*exp(c1*t)`: can match `-0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t)` ✓
- `c2`: constant term (set to 0)
- `c3/(A + c4)**2`: rational term (set c3=0 to eliminate)
- `c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`: This is key!

For the sin term: `c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`

I need this to match `0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`.

Set c6=1, c7=1, c8=0, c5=0.94264. Then: `0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))` ✓

But wait - the GT also has `-0.25667*A` (the linear term without exponential). Candidate 19 doesn't have a standalone linear `A` term. Let me check again...

The GT is: `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A+1))`

Candidate 19 has `A*c0*exp(c1*t)` which gives one `A*exp(ct)` term, but I need BOTH `A` and `A*exp(ct)`. These are linearly independent, so one `A*exp(c1*t)` term can't produce both (unless c1=0, but then I lose the exponential).

Candidate 19 doesn't have a separate linear A term. So it can't match.

**Candidate 33**: `A**2*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6) + c7*log(A*c8 + 1)`

This has `A*c3` for the linear term and `A*c1*exp(c2*t)` for the exponential term. But the sin term is `sin(A*c5 + c6)`, not `sin(log(A+1))`. Can't match.

**Candidate 27**: `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5/(A + c6)**2`

Has `A*c0` and `A*c1*exp(c2*t)`, but `log(A*c4+1)` instead of `sin(log(A+1))`. Can't match.

Let me reconsider **Candidate 19** more carefully. Could the `c3/(A+c4)**2` term somehow combine with something to produce the linear `A` term? No, `1/(A+c4)^2` is fundamentally different from `A`.

**Candidate 37**: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A**c2*c3 + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6)`

Actually, I don't see any candidate that simultaneously has: (1) `A` term, (2) `A*exp(ct)` term, and (3) `sin(log(A+c))` term.

None of the candidates can produce all three required functional forms simultaneously.

GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

This has three terms:
1. A linear term in A: `-0.25667*A`
2. A term `A*exp(-0.02054*t)` with coefficient `-0.25667`
3. A term `sin(log(A + 1))` with coefficient `0.94264`

The key basis functions are: `A`, `A*exp(c*t)`, and `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these basis functions, especially `sin(log(A+1))` which is very specific.

**Candidates with sin terms:** 15, 19, 33, 37

**Candidate 15:** `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2 + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5*sin(A*c6 + c7)`
Has `sin(A*c6 + c7)` not `sin(log(A+1))`. These are different basis functions. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 19:** `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2 + c3/(A+c4)^2 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1) + c8)`
This has `sin(c6*log(A*c7+1) + c8)`. Set c6=1, c7=1, c8=0 → `sin(log(A+1))`. Also has `A*c0*exp(c1*t)` which can give the exponential decay term. But we need a linear `A` term. The term `c3/(A+c4)^2` cannot produce a linear `A` term. Set c2=0, c3=0. Then we get `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c5*sin(log(A+1))`. This gives `A*exp(c1*t)` but not separate `A` and `A*exp(c*t)` terms. We need both `A` and `A*exp(c*t)` independently. With only one `A*exp(c1*t)` term, we can't split it into `A + A*exp(c*t)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 33:** `A^2*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c4*sin(A*c5+c6) + c7*log(A*c8+1)`
Has `sin(A*c5+c6)` not `sin(log(A+1))`, and `log(A*c8+1)` not `sin(log(...))`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 37:** `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A^c2*c3 + c4*sin(A*c5+c6)`
Has `sin(A*c5+c6)` not `sin(log(A+1))`. **NO MATCH**

For all other candidates without a `sin(log(...))` term: The GT contains `sin(log(A+1))` which is a transcendental function that cannot be represented by polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, or logarithms alone. Since `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all these basis functions, no combination of them can reproduce it exactly.

Let me verify candidates with `log` terms: `log(A+1)` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))`. These are different functions.

Candidates with `exp(A*c)` terms also cannot match `sin(log(A+1))`.

None of the candidates contain the required `sin(log(A+c))` basis function (except Candidate 19 which has it but lacks the ability to produce both `A` and `A*exp(c*t)` independently — actually wait, let me recheck 19).

**Candidate 19 recheck:** `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2 + c3/(A+c4)^2 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1)+c8)`
We need `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t)`. Can we write `-0.25667*A(1+exp(-0.02054*t))` as `A*c0*exp(c1*t)`? No, because `A*(1+exp(c*t))` requires two terms. We only have one `A*exp` term and no standalone `A` term. The `c3/(A+c4)^2` term cannot equal `c*A`. **NO MATCH confirmed.**
